</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><div><dl class="temp-labeled-list small"><dt></dt><dd><div><p class="no_margin">AD = <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a>; MOI = <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/mode-of-inheritance/">mode of inheritance</a>; OT = occupational therapy; PT = physical therapy</p></div></dd><dt>1. </dt><dd><div id="cmt2c.TF.6b.1"><p class="no_margin">Clinical geneticist, certified genetic counselor, certified genetic nurse, genetics advanced practice provider (nurse practitioner or physician assistant)</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div></div><div id="cmt2c.Treatment_of_Manifestations"><h3>Treatment of Manifestations</h3><p>Treatment is focused on symptom management. Affected individuals are often evaluated and managed by a multidisciplinary team that includes neurologists, physiatrists, orthopedic surgeons, otologists/audiologists, laryngologists, pulmonologists, geneticists, and physical and occupational therapists.</p><div id="cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4" class="table"><h3><span class="label">Table 7a. </span></h3><div class="caption"><p>Autosomal Dominant <i>TRPV4-</i>Related Neuromuscular Disorder: Treatment of Manifestations</p></div><p class="large-table-link" style="display:none"><span class="right"><a href="/books/NBK201366/table/cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4/?report=objectonly" target="object">View in own window</a></span></p><div class="large_tbl" id="__cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_lrgtbl__"><table class="no_bottom_margin"><thead><tr><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_1" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Manifestation/Concern</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_2" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Treatment</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_3" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Considerations/Other</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Neuropathy</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Special shoes, incl those w/good ankle support; shoe orthotics</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>AFO/KAFO to correct foot drop &#x00026; aid walking</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Orthopedic surgery to correct severe pes cavus deformity or joint contractures as needed</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Forearm crutches, canes/walkers for gait stability, &#x00026; wheelchairs</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Exercise w/in person's capability (Many remain physically active.)</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>PT/OT to address hand &#x00026; leg weakness</div></li></ul>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"></td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Kyphoscoliosis</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Orthopedic eval w/consideration of surgical intervention (e.g., spinal fusion)</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">If kyphoscoliosis results in pain &#x00026;/or compromised pulmonary function</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_4_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

<b>Odontoid hypoplasia&#x000a0;/</b>
<br />
<b>Cervical myelopathy</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Occipitocervical or upper cervical decompression &#x00026; fusion are required to stabilize upper cervical spine &#x00026; relieve cervical cord compression when upper cervical spine instability is documented or when clinical findings of cervical myelopathy are present.</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">It is preferred that intervention in children occurs when signs of cervical compression are present by MRI (even in absence of symptoms) to minimize neurologic injury &#x00026; maximize function. Those undergoing surgical fusion typically do well; minor secondary complications can incl pin site infections, pressure sores, &#x00026; long-term difficulty w/endotracheal intubation.</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">If myelopathy is suspected:
<ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Obtain cervical spine radiographs &#x00026; MRI</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Refer for eval by pediatric orthopedic surgeon or neurosurgeon at tertiary care facility.</div></li></ul>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Upper cervical instability may result in deteriorating endurance &#x00026; worsening gait.</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Standard treatments incl nutritional support</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"></td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Pain &#x00026; depression</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Symptomatic treatment</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_5_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Chronic pain mgmt preceding or following orthopedic surgery is standard &#x00026; often required.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><div><dl class="temp-labeled-list small"><dt></dt><dd><div><p class="no_margin">PT = physical therapy; SNHL = sensorineural hearing loss</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div></div><div id="cmt2c.Surveillance"><h3>Surveillance</h3><div id="cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6" class="table"><h3><span class="label">Table 8a. </span></h3><div class="caption"><p>Autosomal Dominant <i>TRPV4-</i>Related Neuromuscular Disorder: Recommended Surveillance</p></div><p class="large-table-link" style="display:none"><span class="right"><a href="/books/NBK201366/table/cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6/?report=objectonly" target="object">View in own window</a></span></p><div class="large_tbl" id="__cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_lrgtbl__"><table class="no_bottom_margin"><thead><tr><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_1" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">System/Concern</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_2" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Evaluation</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_3" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Frequency</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_1" rowspan="2" scope="rowgroup" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Neurologic exam to determine extent of weakness &#x00026; atrophy, &#x00026; sensory loss</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_3" rowspan="6" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Annually</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="col" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">PT exam to monitor feet to determine need for bracing, special shoes, &#x00026;/or surgery</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Vocal cord involvement</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">ENT consultation w/laryngoscopy</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Respiratory dysfunction</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Dynamic breathing chest radiograph &#x00026; spirometry, sleep study</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>SNHL</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Hearing assessment</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Musculoskeletal</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Assess for joint contractures, hip dysplasia, scoliosis, &#x00026; manifestations of tethered spinal cord.</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

<b>Constitutional</b>

</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Assess weight, height, &#x00026; weight-for-height.</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_6_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">At each visit</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><div><dl class="temp-labeled-list small"><dt></dt><dd><div><p class="no_margin">ENT = otolaryngology; PT = physical therapy; SNHL = sensorineural hearing loss</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div><div id="cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7" class="table"><h3><span class="label">Table 8b. </span></h3><div class="caption"><p>Autosomal Dominant <i>TRPV4-</i>Related Skeletal Dysplasia: Recommended Surveillance</p></div><p class="large-table-link" style="display:none"><span class="right"><a href="/books/NBK201366/table/cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7/?report=objectonly" target="object">View in own window</a></span></p><div class="large_tbl" id="__cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_lrgtbl__"><table class="no_bottom_margin"><thead><tr><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_1" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">System/Concern</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_2" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Evaluation</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_3" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Frequency</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_1" rowspan="2" scope="rowgroup" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Musculoskeletal</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Assessment for development of joint pain &#x00026; scoliosis</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Annually</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Cervical spinal films to assess for clinically significant odontoid hypoplasia</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Before:
<ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>A child reaches school age;</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Surgical procedures involving general anesthesia.</div></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>SNHL</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Hearing assessment</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Annually</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

<b>Constitutional</b>

</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Assess weight, height, &#x00026; weight-for-height</td><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.autosomal_dominant_trpv4related_7_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">At each visit</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><div><dl class="temp-labeled-list small"><dt></dt><dd><div><p class="no_margin">SNHL = sensorineural hearing loss</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div></div><div id="cmt2c.AgentsCircumstances_to_Avoid"><h3>Agents/Circumstances to Avoid</h3><p>In general, obesity is to be avoided because it makes walking more difficult for individuals with neuropathy, skeletal dysplasia, or both.</p><p>
<b>For neuromuscular disorders</b>
</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Preventive health care to avoid diabetes-related complications is recommended.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Neurotoxic medications should be avoided. Medications that are toxic or potentially toxic to persons with Charcot-Marie-Tooth disease (CMT) comprise a spectrum of risk ranging from definite high risk to negligible risk. See the Charcot-Marie-Tooth Association <a href="https://www.cmtausa.org/living-with-cmt/managing-cmt/medications/" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">website</a> (pdf) for an up-to-date list. See also the Inherited Neuropathy Consortium <a href="https://www.rarediseasesnetwork.org/cms/inc/" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">website</a> for additional information.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Upper respiratory tract infections can cause vocal fold swelling and worsen upper airway obstruction.</div></li></ul><p>
<b>For skeletal dysplasias</b>
</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>In individuals with odontoid hypoplasia, avoid extreme neck flexion and extension.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Avoid activities and occupations that place undue stress on the spine and weight-bearing joints.</div></li></ul></div><div id="cmt2c.Evaluation_of_Relatives_at_Risk"><h3>Evaluation of Relatives at Risk</h3><p>See <a href="#cmt2c.Related_Genetic_Counseling_Issues">Genetic Counseling</a> for issues related to testing of at-risk relatives for <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/genetic-counseling/">genetic counseling</a> purposes.</p></div><div id="cmt2c.Pregnancy_Management"><h3>Pregnancy Management</h3><p>There is no registry or data regarding the frequency or outcome of pregnancies in women with an <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> <i>TRPV4</i>-related disorder; however, the following general information may be reasonable to consider. Ideally a woman with an autosomal dominant <i>TRPV4-</i>related disorder would seek consultation from a high-risk obstetrician or maternal-fetal medicine specialist to evaluate her risks for pregnancy and delivery. Increased risk of ectopic pregnancy has been reported [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.li.2019.77">Li et al 2019</a>].</p><p><b>Autosomal dominant</b>
<b><i>TRPV4-</i>related neuromuscular disorders.</b> Results of an Italian registry observed higher rates of placenta previa, abnormal presentations, and preterm deliveries in all forms of CMT, but pregnancy outcome and newborn weight and health were similar to those of the reference populations [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.pisciotta.2020.e3180">Pisciotta et al 2020</a>]. Additionally, a retrospective review in European pregnancies for inherited neuromuscular disorders demonstrated common complications such as polyhydramnios, preterm labor, miscarriages, and cesarean sections. Specifically, CMT and limb-girdle muscular dystrophy were associated with preterm labor and cesarean deliveries [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.ahmed.2025.152">Ahmed et al 2025</a>]. <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.argov.2009.675">Argov &#x00026; de Visser [2009]</a> reviewed pregnancy issues in hereditary neuromuscular disorders including CMT. About 50% of women with CMT described increased weakness during pregnancy that usually resolved post partum [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.rudniksch_neborn.1993.2011">Rudnik-Sch&#x000f6;neborn et al 1993</a>]. Operative deliveries were reported more commonly in women with CMT in Norway [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.hoff.2005.459">Hoff et al 2005</a>]. <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.greenwood.2007.149">Greenwood &#x00026; Scott [2007]</a> described the obstetric approach to women with mild and severe forms of CMT. <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.brock.2009.335">Brock et al [2009]</a> describe use of anesthesia during delivery in a single case study, indicating that regional management is the preferred and safer method, compared to general anesthesia. A German study reviewed 63 pregnancies in 33 women with CMT [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.awater.2012.153">Awater et al 2012</a>] and found no increase in the frequency of cesarean section, forceps delivery, premature birth, or neonatal problems. About one third of mothers felt a worsening of CMT symptoms during pregnancy; in one fifth of mothers the changes were felt to be persistent [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.pisciotta.2020.e3180">Pisciotta et al 2020</a>].</p><p><b>Autosomal dominant</b>
<b><i>TRPV4-</i>related skeletal dysplasias.</b> In <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> <i>TRPV4-</i>related skeletal dysplasias, the degree of pulmonary compromise (from the short trunk and decreased lung capacity) may affect the ability to carry a pregnancy to term. Thus, it is unlikely that a woman with metatropic dysplasia could carry a pregnancy. Pregnant women with a <i>TRPV4-</i>related skeletal dysplasia generally undergo cesarean section delivery because of the small size of the pelvis. Best practice guidelines for prenatal evaluation and delivery of women with skeletal dysplasia have been published [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.savarirayan.2018.545">Savarirayan et al 2018</a>].</p><p>See <a href="https://www.mothertobaby.org/" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">MotherToBaby</a> for further information on medication use during pregnancy.</p></div><div id="cmt2c.Therapies_Under_Investigation"><h3>Therapies Under Investigation</h3><p><a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.de_grado.2025.427">De Grado et al [2025]</a> have reviewed the future of therapeutic options in CMT.</p><p>Preclinical studies in knock-in mouse models of <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disease have shown that small-molecule TRPV4 (transient receptor potential cation channel subfamily V member 4) ion channel antagonists result in improvement in disease phenotypes [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.sullivan.2024.eadk1358">Sullivan et al 2024</a>]. Based on these studies and the known mechanism of disease, TRPV4-specific ion channel antagonists are under study as a potential therapy for <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disease.</p><p>Search <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">ClinicalTrials.gov</a> in the US and <a href="https://www.clinicaltrialsregister.eu/ctr-search/search" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">EU Clinical Trials Register</a> in Europe for access to information on clinical studies for a wide range of diseases and conditions. Note: There may not be clinical trials for this disorder.</p></div><div id="cmt2c.Other"><h3>Other</h3><p>Career and employment choices may be influenced by persistent weakness of hands and/or feet and orthopedic involvement.</p></div></div><div id="cmt2c.Genetic_Counseling"><h2 id="_cmt2c_Genetic_Counseling_">Genetic Counseling</h2><div id="cmt2c.Mode_of_Inheritance"><h3>Mode of Inheritance</h3><p>By definition, <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> <i>TRPV4</i>-related disorders are inherited in an autosomal dominant manner.</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Clinically recognized <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disorders are Charcot-Marie-Tooth disease type 2C, scapuloperoneal spinal muscular atrophy, and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/congenital/">congenital</a> distal spinal muscular atrophy.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Clinically recognized <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> <i>TRPV4</i>-related skeletal dysplasias are <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/familial/">familial</a> digital arthropathy with brachydactyly, brachyolmia, spondylometaphyseal dysplasia (Kozlowski type), spondyloepimetaphyseal dysplasia (Maroteaux type), and metatropic dysplasia.</div></li></ul><p>Note: The <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> p.Ser94Leu has been associated with <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-recessive/">autosomal recessive</a> <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disease (see <a href="#cmt2c.Genetically_Related_Allelic_Disord">Genetically Related Disorders</a>).</p></div><div id="cmt2c.Risk_to_Family_Members"><h3>Risk to Family Members</h3><p>
<b>Parents of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a></b>
</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Because the most severe <i>TRPV4-</i>related skeletal phenotypes can be lethal in childhood (or in utero), children with these phenotypes typically have a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/de-novo/"><i>de novo</i></a> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> and unaffected parents.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Individuals with less severe skeletal phenotypes or neuromuscular phenotypes often have the disorder as the result of a <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> inherited from a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/heterozygous/">heterozygous</a> parent. (Note: A heterozygous parent may appear asymptomatic or have more or less severe clinical manifestations than the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a>; see <a href="#cmt2c.Penetrance">Penetrance</a> and <a href="#cmt2c.GenotypePhenotype_Correlations">Genotype-Phenotype Correlations</a>.) <i>De novo</i> pathogenic variants have also been described in individuals with these phenotypes.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> appears to be the only affected family member (i.e., a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/simplex/">simplex</a> case), <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/molecular-genetic-testing/">molecular genetic testing</a> is recommended for the parents of the proband to evaluate their genetic status and inform <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/recurrence-risk/">recurrence risk</a> assessment. Note: Evaluation of parents may determine that one is affected but has escaped previous diagnosis because of a milder <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/phenotype/">phenotype</a> (possibly associated with parental <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/mosaicism/">mosaicism</a>) or reduced <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/penetrance/">penetrance</a> in the parent with the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>. Therefore, <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/de-novo/"><i>de novo</i></a> occurrence of a <i>TRPV4</i> pathogenic variant cannot be confirmed unless molecular genetic testing has demonstrated that neither parent has the <i>TRPV4</i> pathogenic variant.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> identified in the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> is not identified in either parent and parental identity testing has confirmed biological maternity and paternity, the following possibilities should be considered:</div><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div class="half_rhythm">The <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> has a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/de-novo/"><i>de novo</i></a> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div class="half_rhythm">The <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> inherited a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> from a parent with gonadal (or somatic and gonadal) <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/mosaicism/">mosaicism</a>.* Note: Testing of parental leukocyte DNA may not detect all instances of <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/somatic-mosaicism/">somatic mosaicism</a> and will not detect a pathogenic variant that is present in the germ (gonadal) cells only.</div><div class="half_rhythm">*&#x000a0;A parent with somatic and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/gonadal-mosaicism/">gonadal mosaicism</a> for a <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> may be mildly/minimally affected.</div></li></ul></li></ul><p><b>Sibs of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a>.</b> The risk to the sibs of the proband depends on the genetic status of the proband's parents:</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If a parent of the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> is affected and/or is known to have the <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> identified in the proband, the risk to the sibs of inheriting the pathogenic variant is 50%.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>The specific <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/phenotype/">phenotype</a>, age of onset, and disease severity cannot be predicted accurately in a sib who inherits a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/familial/">familial</a> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> because of reduced <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/penetrance/">penetrance</a> and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/variable-expressivity/">variable expressivity</a>. A <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/heterozygous/">heterozygous</a> sib may have the same phenotype as the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> or have less severe or more severe clinical manifestations (see <a href="#cmt2c.Penetrance">Penetrance</a> and <a href="#cmt2c.GenotypePhenotype_Correlations">Genotype-Phenotype Correlations</a>).</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If the <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> identified in the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> cannot be detected in the leukocyte DNA of either parent, the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/recurrence-risk/">recurrence risk</a> to sibs is estimated to be 1% because of the possibility of parental <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/gonadal-mosaicism/">gonadal mosaicism</a> [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.rahbari.2016.126">Rahbari et al 2016</a>].</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If the parents have not been tested for the <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> but are clinically unaffected, sibs are still presumed to be at increased risk for a <i>TRPV4-</i>related disorder because of the possibility of reduced <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/penetrance/">penetrance</a> in a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/heterozygous/">heterozygous</a> parent and the possibility of parental <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/gonadal-mosaicism/">gonadal mosaicism</a>.</div></li></ul><p>
<b>Offspring of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a></b>
</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Each child of an individual with an <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> <i>TRPV4-</i>related disorder has a 50% chance of inheriting the <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>. Specific <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/phenotype/">phenotype</a>, age of onset, and disease severity cannot be predicted accurately because of reduced <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/penetrance/">penetrance</a> and highly <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/variable-expressivity/">variable expressivity</a>. However, in general, a child who inherits a <i>TRPV4</i> pathogenic variant associated with neuromuscular disease or skeletal dysplasia from an affected parent is likely to have a similar overall phenotype as the parent, although age of onset and severity may be quite distinct.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Because many individuals with short stature have reproductive partners with short stature, offspring of individuals with an <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> <i>TRPV4</i>-related skeletal disorder may be at risk of having <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/double-heterozygosity/">double heterozygosity</a> for two dominantly inherited bone growth disorders. The phenotypes of these individuals may be distinct from those of the parents. If the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> and the proband's reproductive partner are affected with different dominantly inherited skeletal dysplasias, each child has a 25% likelihood of having average stature, a 25% likelihood of having the same skeletal dysplasia as the father, a 25% likelihood of having the same skeletal dysplasia as the mother, and a 25% likelihood of inheriting a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> from both parents and being at risk for a potentially poor outcome.</div></li></ul><p><b>Other family members.</b> The risk to other family members depends on the status of the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a>'s parents: if a parent has the <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>, the parent's family members may be at risk.</p></div><div id="cmt2c.Related_Genetic_Counseling_Issues"><h3>Related Genetic Counseling Issues</h3><p>
<b>Family planning</b>
</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>The optimal time for determination of genetic risk and discussion of the availability of prenatal/<a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/preimplantation-genetic-testing/">preimplantation genetic testing</a> is before pregnancy.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>It is appropriate to offer <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/genetic-counseling/">genetic counseling</a> (including discussion of potential risks to offspring and reproductive options) to young adults who are affected or at risk.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Genetic counseling is recommended when both parents have a skeletal dysplasia.</div></li></ul><p>
<b>Predictive testing (i.e., testing of asymptomatic at-risk individuals)</b>
</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Predictive testing for at-risk relatives is possible once the <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> has been identified in an affected family member. Further clinical evaluation, electromyography&#x000a0;/ nerve conduction velocity testing, and/or skeletal survey may be appropriate for individuals found to have a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/familial/">familial</a> pathogenic variant. No disease-modifying treatment is available to individuals early in the course of the disease. Thus, such testing is for personal decision making only.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Potential consequences of such testing (including, but not limited to, socioeconomic changes and the need for long-term follow up and evaluation arrangements for individuals with a positive test result) as well as the capabilities and limitations of predictive testing should be discussed in the context of formal <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/genetic-counseling/">genetic counseling</a> prior to testing.</div></li></ul><p><b>Predictive testing in minors (i.e., testing of asymptomatic at-risk individuals younger than age 18 years)</b> for a condition that may be adult-onset and for which early treatment would have no beneficial effect on disease morbidity and mortality should be discussed in the context of formal <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/genetic-counseling/">genetic counseling</a>. The autonomy of the minor is a primary concern and consideration should be given to delay of predictive genetic testing until the at-risk individual is capable of informed decision making.</p><p>In a family with an established diagnosis of a <i>TRPV4-</i>related disorder, it is appropriate to consider testing of symptomatic individuals regardless of age.</p></div><div id="cmt2c.Prenatal_Testing_and_Preimplantati"><h3>Prenatal Testing and Preimplantation Genetic Testing</h3><p>Once the <i>TRPV4</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> has been identified in an affected family member, prenatal and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/preimplantation-genetic-testing/">preimplantation genetic testing</a> are possible. However, specific <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/phenotype/">phenotype</a>, age of onset, and/or disease severity cannot be reliably predicted based on the results of <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/prenatal-testing/">prenatal testing</a>.</p><p>Differences in perspective may exist among medical professionals and within families regarding the use of prenatal and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/preimplantation-genetic-testing/">preimplantation genetic testing</a>. While most health care professionals would consider use of prenatal and preimplantation genetic testing to be a personal decision, discussion of these issues may be helpful.</p></div></div><div <a href="/omim/184252" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">184252</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">SPONDYLOMETAPHYSEAL DYSPLASIA, KOZLOWSKI TYPE; SMDK</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<a href="/omim/600175" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">600175</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">NEURONOPATHY, DISTAL HEREDITARY MOTOR, AUTOSOMAL DOMINANT 8; HMND8</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<a href="/omim/605427" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">605427</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">TRANSIENT RECEPTOR POTENTIAL CATION CHANNEL, SUBFAMILY V, MEMBER 4; TRPV4</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<a href="/omim/606071" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">606071</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">HEREDITARY MOTOR AND SENSORY NEUROPATHY, TYPE IIC; HMSN2C</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<a href="/omim/606835" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">606835</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">DIGITAL ARTHROPATHY-BRACHYDACTYLY, FAMILIAL; FDAB</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div id="cmt2c.Molecular_Pathogenesis"><h3>Molecular Pathogenesis</h3><p><i>TRPV4</i> encodes transient receptor potential cation channel subfamily V member 4 (TRPV4), a nonselective Ca2+-permeable cation channel that is predominantly expressed at the plasma membrane [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.rosenbaum.2020.3837">Rosenbaum et al 2020</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.toftbertelsen.2021.165">Toft-Bertelsen &#x00026; MacAulay 2021</a>]. TRPV4 can be activated by a wide range of stimuli including hypo-osmolarity, heat, and mechanical stretch, as well as numerous endogenous (e.g., endocannabinoid anandamide, arachidonic acid) and synthetic (4&#x003b1;-phorbol-12,13-didecanoate [4&#x003b1;PDD]) compounds [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.garciaelias.2014.293">Garcia-Elias et al 2014</a>]. TRPV4 is broadly expressed and has diverse physiologic roles in different tissue types:</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Osmosensation and flow sensing in the kidney [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.rosenbaum.2020.3837">Rosenbaum et al 2020</a>]</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Endothelial barrier function and vascular tone in the cerebral and pulmonary vasculature [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.kuppusamy.2021.136258">Kuppusamy et al 2021</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.sonkusare.2022.43">Sonkusare &#x00026; Laubach 2022</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.lambrichts.2025.107492">Lambrichts et al 2025</a>]</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Mechanosensation and nociception in the sensory nervous system [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.tominaga.2024.3">Tominaga &#x00026; Kashio 2024</a>]</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Bladder sensation and function [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.wu.2021.39">Wu et al 2021</a>]</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Skin homeostasis and function [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.rosenbaum.2020.3837">Rosenbaum et al 2020</a>]</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Chondrogenesis and bone homeostasis [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.toftbertelsen.2021.165">Toft-Bertelsen &#x00026; MacAulay 2021</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.liu.2022.577">Liu et al 2022</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.zhang.2022.237">Zhang et al 2022</a>]</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Immune function and inflammation [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.michalick.2020.413">Michalick &#x00026; Kuebler 2020</a>]</div></li></ul><p>While the precise mechanisms of pathogenesis in <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> <i>TRPV4-</i>related disorders are not completely understood, the preponderance of evidence suggests that pathogenic variants cause disease through gain of ion channel function [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.nilius.2013.152">Nilius &#x00026; Voets 2013</a>]. TRPV4 is a cell surface-expressed cation channel and principally fluxes calcium. Given the diverse signaling pathways regulated by intracellular calcium influx, many possible downstream pathologic events are conceivable, including activation of calcium-sensitive proteases (such as calpains) or kinases (such as CaMKII), alterations in calcium-sensitive transcriptional programs, and dysregulation of cytoskeletal remodeling. In addition, the downstream consequences of TRPV4 gain of channel function are likely to be dependent on cell type- and tissue-specific factors.</p><p><b>Mechanism of disease causation.</b> Autosomal dominant <i>TRPV4-</i>related disorders are diverse but are likely linked through gain of TRPV4 ion channel function with tissue-specific downstream consequences. Notably, the vast majority of pathogenic variants reported are <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/missense/">missense</a> variants.</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div><b>Neuromuscular disorders.</b> Gain of ion channel function of multiple pathogenic variants has been demonstrated in vitro and in fly and mouse models of disease [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.deng.2010.165">Deng et al 2010</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.landour_.2010.170">Landour&#x000e9; et al 2010</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.klein.2011.887">Klein et al 2011</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.sullivan.2015.e29">Sullivan et al 2015</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.woolums.2020.2679">Woolums et al 2020</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.sullivan.2024.eadk1358">Sullivan et al 2024</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.kosmanopoulos.2025.238">Kosmanopoulos et al 2025</a>]. Notably, <i>Trpv4</i> knock-in mice develop a severe, rapidly progressive fatal neuromuscular <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/phenotype/">phenotype</a> that can be rescued by pharmacologic inhibition of TRPV4 ion channel activity [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.sullivan.2024.eadk1358">Sullivan et al 2024</a>]. In addition, this phenotype is associated with breakdown of blood-brain and blood-spinal cord barriers due to expression of mutated TRPV4 in neural vascular endothelial cells [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.sullivan.2024.eadk1358">Sullivan et al 2024</a>]. These findings suggest that disruption of neural vascular barriers could contribute to disease pathogenesis, although such a mechanism has not been demonstrated in affected individuals.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div><b>Skeletal dysplasias.</b> The vast majority of skeletal dysplasia pathogenic variants are <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/missense/">missense</a> variants that are believed to cause gain of function, although frameshift and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/deletion/">deletion</a> variants have been reported [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.dai.2010.704">Dai et al 2010</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.nishimura.2010.1443">Nishimura et al 2010</a>]. Like pathogenic variants associated with neuromuscular disorders, skeletal dysplasia-associated variants also generally cause increased basal calcium influx [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.loukin.2011.e19533">Loukin et al 2011</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.taga.2022.375">Taga et al 2022</a>]. The precise downstream pathogenic events remain unknown, although reduced bone morphogenic protein signaling with resultant impairment in endochondral ossification has been proposed based on in vitro studies and a knock-in mouse model [<a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.leddy.2014a.e962971">Leddy et al 2014a</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.leddy.2014b.2525">Leddy et al 2014b</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.dicks.2023.e71154">Dicks et al 2023</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#cmt2c.REF.harissa.2025.c1135">Harissa et al 2025</a>].</div></li></ul><div id="cmt2c.T.trpv4_pathogenic_variants_refere" class="table"><h3><span class="label">Table 9. </span></h3><div class="caption"><p><i>TRPV4</i> Pathogenic Variants Referenced in This <i>GeneReview</i></p></div><p class="large-table-link" style="display:none"><span class="right"><a href="/books/NBK201366/table/cmt2c.T.trpv4_pathogenic_variants_refere/?report=objectonly" target="object">View in own window</a></span></p><div class="large_tbl" id="__cmt2c.T.trpv4_pathogenic_variants_refere_lrgtbl__"><table class="no_bottom_margin"><thead><tr><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.trpv4_pathogenic_variants_refere_1_1_1_1" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Reference Sequences</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.trpv4_pathogenic_variants_refere_1_1_1_2" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">DNA Nucleotide Change</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.trpv4_pathogenic_variants_refere_1_1_1_3" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Predicted Protein Change</th><th id="hd_h_cmt2c.T.trpv4_pathogenic_variants_refere_1_1_1_4" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Comment [Reference]</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td headers="hd_h_cmt2c.T.trpv4_pathogenic_variants_refere_1_1_1_1" rowspan="14" scope="rowgroup" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

class="no_margin"><i>GeneReviews</i> follows the standard naming conventions of the Human Genome Variation Society (<a href="https://varnomen.hgvs.org/" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">varnomen<wbr style="display:inline-block"></wbr>​.hgvs.org</a>). See <a href="/books/n/gene/app3/">Quick Reference</a> for an explanation of nomenclature.</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div></div></div><div id="cmt2c.Chapter_Notes"><h2 id="_cmt2c_Chapter_Notes_">Chapter Notes</h2><div id="cmt2c.Author_Notes"><h3>Author Notes</h3><p><b>Brett A McCray, MD, PhD,</b> is a physician-scientist at the University of Michigan who leads a basic, translational, and clinical research program. His research is focused on furthering the understanding and treatment of hereditary neuropathy with a primary focus on <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disease. The lab uses cultured cells and animal models to elucidate pathways important in the pathogenesis of <i>TRPV4</i>-related disease and other forms of neuropathy. The lab is also involved in clinical and translational research efforts to help bring insights from the bench to individuals with <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disease.</p><p><b>Charlotte J Sumner, MD,</b> is a physician-scientist at Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine who studies and cares for individuals with genetic motor neuron and peripheral nerve diseases. Her laboratory discovered <i>TRPV4</i> pathogenic variants that cause neuromuscular disease, developed cell and animal models of disease, and demonstrated that TRPV4 small-molecule antagonists can ameliorate disease features in these models. She is leading ongoing clinical studies of individuals with <i>TRPV4</i> pathogenic variants at Johns Hopkins University.</p><p>Dr McCray (<a href="mailto:dev@null" data-email="ude.hcimu.dem@yarccmb" class="oemail">ude.hcimu.dem@yarccmb</a>) and Dr Sumner (<a href="mailto:dev@null" data-email="ude.imhj@1renmusc" class="oemail">ude.imhj@1renmusc</a>) are actively involved in clinical research regarding individuals with <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disease. They would be happy to communicate with persons who have any questions regarding diagnosis of <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disease or other considerations.</p><p>Dr McCray and Dr Sumner are also interested in hearing from clinicians treating families affected by <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular disease in whom no causative variant has been identified through <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/molecular-genetic-testing/">molecular genetic testing</a> of the genes known to be involved in this group of disorders.</p><p>Contact Dr McCray or Dr Sumner to inquire about review of <i>TRPV4</i> variants of <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/uncertain-significance/">uncertain significance</a>.</p></div><div id="cmt2c.Acknowledgments"><h3>Acknowledgments</h3><p>Research on <i>TRPV4</i>-related neuromuscular diseases has been supported by the Inherited Neuropathies Consortium, NINDS, the Muscular Dystrophy Association, Actio Biosciences, and by individuals and families affected by the condition, particularly the TRPV4 Related Hereditary Neuropathies Facebook group led by Stephanie Carmody.</p></div><div id="cmt2c.Revision_History"><h3>Revision History</h3><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>4 December 2025 (sw) Comprehensive update posted live</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>17 September 2020 (sw) Comprehensive update posted live</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>15 May 2014 (me) Review posted live</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>30 July 2013 (as) Original submission</div></li></ul></div></div><div id="cmt2c.References"><h2 id="_cmt2c_References_">References</h2><div id="cmt2c.Literature_Cited"><h3>Literature Cited</h3><ul class="simple-list"><li class="half_rhythm"><div class="bk_ref" id="cmt2c.REF.ahmed.2025.152">Ahmed

    (function($){
        $('.skiplink').each(function(i, item){
            var href = $($(item).attr('href'));
            href.attr('tabindex', '-1').addClass('skiptarget'); // ensure the target can receive focus
            $(item).on('click', function(event){
                event.preventDefault();
                $.scrollTo(href, 0, {
                    onAfter: function(){
                        href.focus();
                    }
                });
            });
        });
    })(jQuery);
